19 Though he knew it would take some hours to get through the forest , he was so anxious to be at his journey 's end that he resolved to go on ; but night overtook him , and the deep snow and bitter frost made it impossible for his horse to carry him any further .
20 Not a house was to be seen ; the only shelter he could get was the hollow trunk of a great tree , and there he crouched all the night which seemed to him the longest he had ever known .
21 In spite of his weariness the howling of the wolves kept him awake , and even when at last the day broke he was not much better off , for the falling snow had covered up every path , and he did not know which XXXXX to turn .	way		age|amusement|expense|merchant|part|peasants|singing|town|trouble|way

1 She had been as sad as anyone when misfortune overtook her father , but , soon recovering her natural gaiety , she set to work to make the best of things , to amuse her father and brothers as well as she could , and to try to persuade her sisters to join her in dancing and singing .
2 But they would do nothing of the sort , and , because she was not as doleful as themselves , they declared that this miserable life was all she was fit for .
3 But she was really far prettier and cleverer than they were ; indeed , she was so lovely that she was always called Beauty .
4 After two years , when they were all beginning to get used to their new life , something happened to disturb their tranquillity .
5 Their father received the news that one of his ships , which he had believed to be lost , had come safely into port with a rich cargo .
6 All the sons and daughters at once thought that their poverty was at an end , and wanted to set out directly for the town ; but their father , who was more prudent , begged them to wait a little , and , though it was harvest time , and he could ill be spared , determined to go himself first , to make inquiries .
7 Only the youngest daughter had any doubt but that they would soon again be as rich as they were before , or at least rich enough to live comfortably in some town where they would find amusement and gay companions once more .
8 So they all loaded their father with commissions for jewels and dresses which it would have taken a fortune to buy ; only Beauty , feeling sure that it was of no use , did not ask for anything .
9 Her father , noticing her silence , said : `` And what shall I bring for you , Beauty ? ''
10 `` The only thing I wish for is to see you come home safely , '' she answered .
11 But this only vexed her sisters , who fancied she was blaming them for having asked for such costly things .
12 Her father , however , was pleased , but as he thought that at her age she certainly ought to like pretty presents , he told her to choose something .
13 `` Well , dear father , '' she said , `` as you insist upon it , I beg that you will bring me a rose .
14 I have not seen one since we came here , and I love them so much . ''
15 So the merchant set out and reached the town as quickly as possible , but only to find that his former companions , believing him to be dead , had divided between them the goods which the ship had brought ; and after six months of trouble and expense he found himself as poor as when he started , having been able to recover only just enough to pay the cost of his journey .
16 To make matters worse , he was obliged to leave the town in the most terrible weather , so that by the time he was within a few leagues of his home he was almost exhausted with cold and fatigue .
17 Though he knew it would take some hours to get through the forest , he was so anxious to be at his journey 's end that he resolved to go on ; but night overtook him , and the deep snow and bitter frost made it impossible for his horse to carry him any further .
18 Not a house was to be seen ; the only shelter he could get was the hollow trunk of a great tree , and there he crouched all the night which seemed to him the longest he had ever known .
19 In spite of his weariness the howling of the wolves kept him awake , and even when at last the day broke he was not much better off , for the falling snow had covered up every path , and he did not know which way to turn .
20 At length he made out some sort of track , and though at the beginning it was so rough and slippery that he fell down more than once , it presently became easier , and led him into an avenue of trees which ended in a splendid castle .
21 It seemed to the XXXXX very strange that no snow had fallen in the avenue , which was entirely composed of orange trees , covered with flowers and fruit .	merchant		dancing|daughter|end|frost|merchant|nothing|silence|tranquillity|way|weather

1 She had been as sad as anyone when misfortune overtook her father , but , soon recovering her natural gaiety , she set to work to make the best of things , to amuse her father and brothers as well as she could , and to try to persuade her sisters to join her in dancing and singing .
2 But they would do nothing of the sort , and , because she was not as doleful as themselves , they declared that this miserable life was all she was fit for .
3 But she was really far prettier and cleverer than they were ; indeed , she was so lovely that she was always called Beauty .
4 After two years , when they were all beginning to get used to their new life , something happened to disturb their tranquillity .
5 Their father received the news that one of his ships , which he had believed to be lost , had come safely into port with a rich cargo .
6 All the sons and daughters at once thought that their poverty was at an end , and wanted to set out directly for the town ; but their father , who was more prudent , begged them to wait a little , and , though it was harvest time , and he could ill be spared , determined to go himself first , to make inquiries .
7 Only the youngest daughter had any doubt but that they would soon again be as rich as they were before , or at least rich enough to live comfortably in some town where they would find amusement and gay companions once more .
8 So they all loaded their father with commissions for jewels and dresses which it would have taken a fortune to buy ; only Beauty , feeling sure that it was of no use , did not ask for anything .
9 Her father , noticing her silence , said : `` And what shall I bring for you , Beauty ? ''
10 `` The only thing I wish for is to see you come home safely , '' she answered .
11 But this only vexed her sisters , who fancied she was blaming them for having asked for such costly things .
12 Her father , however , was pleased , but as he thought that at her age she certainly ought to like pretty presents , he told her to choose something .
13 `` Well , dear father , '' she said , `` as you insist upon it , I beg that you will bring me a rose .
14 I have not seen one since we came here , and I love them so much . ''
15 So the merchant set out and reached the town as quickly as possible , but only to find that his former companions , believing him to be dead , had divided between them the goods which the ship had brought ; and after six months of trouble and expense he found himself as poor as when he started , having been able to recover only just enough to pay the cost of his journey .
16 To make matters worse , he was obliged to leave the town in the most terrible weather , so that by the time he was within a few leagues of his home he was almost exhausted with cold and fatigue .
17 Though he knew it would take some hours to get through the forest , he was so anxious to be at his journey 's end that he resolved to go on ; but night overtook him , and the deep snow and bitter frost made it impossible for his horse to carry him any further .
18 Not a house was to be seen ; the only shelter he could get was the hollow trunk of a great tree , and there he crouched all the night which seemed to him the longest he had ever known .
19 In spite of his weariness the howling of the wolves kept him awake , and even when at last the day broke he was not much better off , for the falling snow had covered up every path , and he did not know which way to turn .
20 At length he made out some sort of track , and though at the beginning it was so rough and slippery that he fell down more than once , it presently became easier , and led him into an avenue of trees which ended in a splendid castle .
21 It seemed to the merchant very strange that no XXXXX had fallen in the avenue , which was entirely composed of orange trees , covered with flowers and fruit .	snow		amusement|cost|daughters|merchant|nothing|ship|snow|something|sort|tree

1 But she was really far prettier and cleverer than they were ; indeed , she was so lovely that she was always called Beauty .
2 After two years , when they were all beginning to get used to their new life , something happened to disturb their tranquillity .
3 Their father received the news that one of his ships , which he had believed to be lost , had come safely into port with a rich cargo .
4 All the sons and daughters at once thought that their poverty was at an end , and wanted to set out directly for the town ; but their father , who was more prudent , begged them to wait a little , and , though it was harvest time , and he could ill be spared , determined to go himself first , to make inquiries .
5 Only the youngest daughter had any doubt but that they would soon again be as rich as they were before , or at least rich enough to live comfortably in some town where they would find amusement and gay companions once more .
6 So they all loaded their father with commissions for jewels and dresses which it would have taken a fortune to buy ; only Beauty , feeling sure that it was of no use , did not ask for anything .
7 Her father , noticing her silence , said : `` And what shall I bring for you , Beauty ? ''
8 `` The only thing I wish for is to see you come home safely , '' she answered .
9 But this only vexed her sisters , who fancied she was blaming them for having asked for such costly things .
10 Her father , however , was pleased , but as he thought that at her age she certainly ought to like pretty presents , he told her to choose something .
11 `` Well , dear father , '' she said , `` as you insist upon it , I beg that you will bring me a rose .
12 I have not seen one since we came here , and I love them so much . ''
13 So the merchant set out and reached the town as quickly as possible , but only to find that his former companions , believing him to be dead , had divided between them the goods which the ship had brought ; and after six months of trouble and expense he found himself as poor as when he started , having been able to recover only just enough to pay the cost of his journey .
14 To make matters worse , he was obliged to leave the town in the most terrible weather , so that by the time he was within a few leagues of his home he was almost exhausted with cold and fatigue .
15 Though he knew it would take some hours to get through the forest , he was so anxious to be at his journey 's end that he resolved to go on ; but night overtook him , and the deep snow and bitter frost made it impossible for his horse to carry him any further .
16 Not a house was to be seen ; the only shelter he could get was the hollow trunk of a great tree , and there he crouched all the night which seemed to him the longest he had ever known .
17 In spite of his weariness the howling of the wolves kept him awake , and even when at last the day broke he was not much better off , for the falling snow had covered up every path , and he did not know which way to turn .
18 At length he made out some sort of track , and though at the beginning it was so rough and slippery that he fell down more than once , it presently became easier , and led him into an avenue of trees which ended in a splendid castle .
19 It seemed to the merchant very strange that no snow had fallen in the avenue , which was entirely composed of orange trees , covered with flowers and fruit .
20 When he reached the first court of the castle he saw before him a flight of agate steps , and went up them , and passed through several splendidly furnished rooms .
21 The pleasant warmth of the air revived him , and he felt very hungry ; but there seemed to be nobody in all this vast and splendid palace whom he could ask to give him XXXXX to eat .	something		age|castle|day|frost|home|merchant|port|silence|something|weather

1 After two years , when they were all beginning to get used to their new life , something happened to disturb their tranquillity .
2 Their father received the news that one of his ships , which he had believed to be lost , had come safely into port with a rich cargo .
3 All the sons and daughters at once thought that their poverty was at an end , and wanted to set out directly for the town ; but their father , who was more prudent , begged them to wait a little , and , though it was harvest time , and he could ill be spared , determined to go himself first , to make inquiries .
4 Only the youngest daughter had any doubt but that they would soon again be as rich as they were before , or at least rich enough to live comfortably in some town where they would find amusement and gay companions once more .
5 So they all loaded their father with commissions for jewels and dresses which it would have taken a fortune to buy ; only Beauty , feeling sure that it was of no use , did not ask for anything .
6 Her father , noticing her silence , said : `` And what shall I bring for you , Beauty ? ''
7 `` The only thing I wish for is to see you come home safely , '' she answered .
8 But this only vexed her sisters , who fancied she was blaming them for having asked for such costly things .
9 Her father , however , was pleased , but as he thought that at her age she certainly ought to like pretty presents , he told her to choose something .
10 `` Well , dear father , '' she said , `` as you insist upon it , I beg that you will bring me a rose .
11 I have not seen one since we came here , and I love them so much . ''
12 So the merchant set out and reached the town as quickly as possible , but only to find that his former companions , believing him to be dead , had divided between them the goods which the ship had brought ; and after six months of trouble and expense he found himself as poor as when he started , having been able to recover only just enough to pay the cost of his journey .
13 To make matters worse , he was obliged to leave the town in the most terrible weather , so that by the time he was within a few leagues of his home he was almost exhausted with cold and fatigue .
14 Though he knew it would take some hours to get through the forest , he was so anxious to be at his journey 's end that he resolved to go on ; but night overtook him , and the deep snow and bitter frost made it impossible for his horse to carry him any further .
15 Not a house was to be seen ; the only shelter he could get was the hollow trunk of a great tree , and there he crouched all the night which seemed to him the longest he had ever known .
16 In spite of his weariness the howling of the wolves kept him awake , and even when at last the day broke he was not much better off , for the falling snow had covered up every path , and he did not know which way to turn .
17 At length he made out some sort of track , and though at the beginning it was so rough and slippery that he fell down more than once , it presently became easier , and led him into an avenue of trees which ended in a splendid castle .
18 It seemed to the merchant very strange that no snow had fallen in the avenue , which was entirely composed of orange trees , covered with flowers and fruit .
19 When he reached the first court of the castle he saw before him a flight of agate steps , and went up them , and passed through several splendidly furnished rooms .
20 The pleasant warmth of the air revived him , and he felt very hungry ; but there seemed to be nobody in all this vast and splendid palace whom he could ask to give him something to eat .
21 Deep XXXXX reigned everywhere , and at last , tired of roaming through empty rooms and galleries , he stopped in a room smaller than the rest , where a clear fire was burning and a couch was drawn up closely to it .	silence		companions|expense|frost|fruit|home|path|rose|silence|something|time

4 Her father , noticing her silence , said : `` And what shall I bring for you , Beauty ? ''
5 `` The only thing I wish for is to see you come home safely , '' she answered .
6 But this only vexed her sisters , who fancied she was blaming them for having asked for such costly things .
7 Her father , however , was pleased , but as he thought that at her age she certainly ought to like pretty presents , he told her to choose something .
8 `` Well , dear father , '' she said , `` as you insist upon it , I beg that you will bring me a rose .
9 I have not seen one since we came here , and I love them so much . ''

15 At length he made out some sort of track , and though at the beginning it was so rough and slippery that he fell down more than once , it presently became easier , and led him into an avenue of trees which ended in a splendid castle .
16 It seemed to the merchant very strange that no snow had fallen in the avenue , which was entirely composed of orange trees , covered with flowers and fruit .
17 When he reached the first court of the castle he saw before him a flight of agate steps , and went up them , and passed through several splendidly furnished rooms .
18 The pleasant warmth of the air revived him , and he felt very hungry ; but there seemed to be nobody in all this vast and splendid palace whom he could ask to give him something to eat .
19 Deep silence reigned everywhere , and at last , tired of roaming through empty rooms and galleries , he stopped in a room smaller than the rest , where a clear fire was burning and a couch was drawn up closely to it .
20 Thinking that this must be prepared for someone who was expected , he sat down to wait till he should come , and very soon fell into a sweet sleep .
21 When his extreme hunger wakened him after several hours , he was still alone ; but a little table , upon which was a good dinner , had been drawn up close to him , and , as he had eaten nothing for twenty-four hours , he lost no XXXXX in beginning his meal , hoping that he might soon have an opportunity of thanking his considerate entertainer , whoever it might be .	time		castle|end|flowers|fruit|sleep|snow|sons|spite|time|weather

6 Her father , however , was pleased , but as he thought that at her age she certainly ought to like pretty presents , he told her to choose something .
7 `` Well , dear father , '' she said , `` as you insist upon it , I beg that you will bring me a rose .
8 I have not seen one since we came here , and I love them so much . ''
9 So the merchant set out and reached the town as quickly as possible , but only to find that his former companions , believing him to be dead , had divided between them the goods which the ship had brought ; and after six months of trouble and expense he found himself as poor as when he started , having been able to recover only just enough to pay the cost of his journey .
10 To make matters worse , he was obliged to leave the town in the most terrible weather , so that by the time he was within a few leagues of his home he was almost exhausted with cold and fatigue .
11 Though he knew it would take some hours to get through the forest , he was so anxious to be at his journey 's end that he resolved to go on ; but night overtook him , and the deep snow and bitter frost made it impossible for his horse to carry him any further .
12 Not a house was to be seen ; the only shelter he could get was the hollow trunk of a great tree , and there he crouched all the night which seemed to him the longest he had ever known .
13 In spite of his weariness the howling of the wolves kept him awake , and even when at last the day broke he was not much better off , for the falling snow had covered up every path , and he did not know which way to turn .
14 At length he made out some sort of track , and though at the beginning it was so rough and slippery that he fell down more than once , it presently became easier , and led him into an avenue of trees which ended in a splendid castle .
15 It seemed to the merchant very strange that no snow had fallen in the avenue , which was entirely composed of orange trees , covered with flowers and fruit .
16 When he reached the first court of the castle he saw before him a flight of agate steps , and went up them , and passed through several splendidly furnished rooms .
17 The pleasant warmth of the air revived him , and he felt very hungry ; but there seemed to be nobody in all this vast and splendid palace whom he could ask to give him something to eat .
18 Deep silence reigned everywhere , and at last , tired of roaming through empty rooms and galleries , he stopped in a room smaller than the rest , where a clear fire was burning and a couch was drawn up closely to it .
19 Thinking that this must be prepared for someone who was expected , he sat down to wait till he should come , and very soon fell into a sweet sleep .
20 When his extreme hunger wakened him after several hours , he was still alone ; but a little table , upon which was a good dinner , had been drawn up close to him , and , as he had eaten nothing for twenty-four hours , he lost no time in beginning his meal , hoping that he might soon have an opportunity of thanking his considerate entertainer , whoever it might be .
21 But no one appeared , and even after another long XXXXX , from which he awoke completely refreshed , there was no sign of anybody , though a fresh meal of dainty cakes and fruit was prepared upon the little table at his elbow .	sleep		couch|court|father|fatigue|forest|horse|path|sisters|sleep|things

16 The pleasant warmth of the air revived him , and he felt very hungry ; but there seemed to be nobody in all this vast and splendid palace whom he could ask to give him something to eat .
17 Deep silence reigned everywhere , and at last , tired of roaming through empty rooms and galleries , he stopped in a room smaller than the rest , where a clear fire was burning and a couch was drawn up closely to it .
18 Thinking that this must be prepared for someone who was expected , he sat down to wait till he should come , and very soon fell into a sweet sleep .
19 When his extreme hunger wakened him after several hours , he was still alone ; but a little table , upon which was a good dinner , had been drawn up close to him , and , as he had eaten nothing for twenty-four hours , he lost no time in beginning his meal , hoping that he might soon have an opportunity of thanking his considerate entertainer , whoever it might be .
20 But no one appeared , and even after another long sleep , from which he awoke completely refreshed , there was no sign of anybody , though a fresh meal of dainty cakes and fruit was prepared upon the little table at his elbow .
21 Being naturally timid , the XXXXX began to terrify him , and he resolved to search once more through all the rooms ; but it was of no use .	silence		air|avenue|castle|opportunity|rose|silence|someone|spite|trees|way

15 When his extreme hunger wakened him after several hours , he was still alone ; but a little table , upon which was a good dinner , had been drawn up close to him , and , as he had eaten nothing for twenty-four hours , he lost no time in beginning his meal , hoping that he might soon have an opportunity of thanking his considerate entertainer , whoever it might be .
16 But no one appeared , and even after another long sleep , from which he awoke completely refreshed , there was no sign of anybody , though a fresh meal of dainty cakes and fruit was prepared upon the little table at his elbow .
17 Being naturally timid , the silence began to terrify him , and he resolved to search once more through all the rooms ; but it was of no use .
18 Not even a servant was to be seen ; there was no sign of life in the palace !
19 He began to wonder what he should do , and to amuse himself by pretending that all the treasures he saw were his own , and considering how he would divide them among his children .
20 Then he went down into the garden , and though it was winter everywhere else , here the sun shone , and the birds sang , and the flowers bloomed , and the air was soft and sweet .
21 The XXXXX , in ecstacies with all he saw and heard , said to himself : `` All this must be meant for me .	merchant		age|forest|goods|home|merchant|nobody|nothing|path|spite|weather

1 `` Well , dear father , '' she said , `` as you insist upon it , I beg that you will bring me a rose .
2 I have not seen one since we came here , and I love them so much . ''
3 So the merchant set out and reached the town as quickly as possible , but only to find that his former companions , believing him to be dead , had divided between them the goods which the ship had brought ; and after six months of trouble and expense he found himself as poor as when he started , having been able to recover only just enough to pay the cost of his journey .
4 To make matters worse , he was obliged to leave the town in the most terrible weather , so that by the time he was within a few leagues of his home he was almost exhausted with cold and fatigue .
5 Though he knew it would take some hours to get through the forest , he was so anxious to be at his journey 's end that he resolved to go on ; but night overtook him , and the deep snow and bitter frost made it impossible for his horse to carry him any further .
6 Not a house was to be seen ; the only shelter he could get was the hollow trunk of a great tree , and there he crouched all the night which seemed to him the longest he had ever known .
7 In spite of his weariness the howling of the wolves kept him awake , and even when at last the day broke he was not much better off , for the falling snow had covered up every path , and he did not know which way to turn .
8 At length he made out some sort of track , and though at the beginning it was so rough and slippery that he fell down more than once , it presently became easier , and led him into an avenue of trees which ended in a splendid castle .
9 It seemed to the merchant very strange that no snow had fallen in the avenue , which was entirely composed of orange trees , covered with flowers and fruit .
10 When he reached the first court of the castle he saw before him a flight of agate steps , and went up them , and passed through several splendidly furnished rooms .
11 The pleasant warmth of the air revived him , and he felt very hungry ; but there seemed to be nobody in all this vast and splendid palace whom he could ask to give him something to eat .
12 Deep silence reigned everywhere , and at last , tired of roaming through empty rooms and galleries , he stopped in a room smaller than the rest , where a clear fire was burning and a couch was drawn up closely to it .
13 Thinking that this must be prepared for someone who was expected , he sat down to wait till he should come , and very soon fell into a sweet sleep .
14 When his extreme hunger wakened him after several hours , he was still alone ; but a little table , upon which was a good dinner , had been drawn up close to him , and , as he had eaten nothing for twenty-four hours , he lost no time in beginning his meal , hoping that he might soon have an opportunity of thanking his considerate entertainer , whoever it might be .
15 But no one appeared , and even after another long sleep , from which he awoke completely refreshed , there was no sign of anybody , though a fresh meal of dainty cakes and fruit was prepared upon the little table at his elbow .
16 Being naturally timid , the silence began to terrify him , and he resolved to search once more through all the rooms ; but it was of no use .
17 Not even a servant was to be seen ; there was no sign of life in the palace !
18 He began to wonder what he should do , and to amuse himself by pretending that all the treasures he saw were his own , and considering how he would divide them among his children .
19 Then he went down into the garden , and though it was winter everywhere else , here the sun shone , and the birds sang , and the flowers bloomed , and the air was soft and sweet .

8 But no one appeared , and even after another long sleep , from which he awoke completely refreshed , there was no sign of anybody , though a fresh meal of dainty cakes and fruit was prepared upon the little table at his elbow .
9 Being naturally timid , the silence began to terrify him , and he resolved to search once more through all the rooms ; but it was of no use .
10 Not even a servant was to be seen ; there was no sign of life in the palace !
11 He began to wonder what he should do , and to amuse himself by pretending that all the treasures he saw were his own , and considering how he would divide them among his children .
12 Then he went down into the garden , and though it was winter everywhere else , here the sun shone , and the birds sang , and the flowers bloomed , and the air was soft and sweet .
13 The merchant , in ecstacies with all he saw and heard , said to himself : `` All this must be meant for me .
14 I will go this minute and bring my children to share all these delights . ''
15 In spite of being so cold and weary when he reached the castle , he had taken his horse to the stable and fed it .
16 Now he thought he would saddle it for his homeward journey , and he turned down the path which led to the stable .
17 This path had a hedge of roses on each side of it , and the merchant thought he had never seen or smelt such exquisite flowers .
18 They reminded him of his promise to Beauty , and he stopped and had just gathered one to take to her when he was startled by a strange noise behind him .
19 Turning round , he saw a frightful Beast , which seemed to be very angry and said , in a terrible voice : `` Who told you that you might gather my roses ?
20 Was it not enough that I allowed you to be in my palace and was kind to you ?
21 This is the way you show your gratitude , by stealing my XXXXX !	flowers		flowers|horse|meal|one|rooms|servant|something|spite|table|voice

1 When he reached the first court of the castle he saw before him a flight of agate steps , and went up them , and passed through several splendidly furnished rooms .
2 The pleasant warmth of the air revived him , and he felt very hungry ; but there seemed to be nobody in all this vast and splendid palace whom he could ask to give him something to eat .
3 Deep silence reigned everywhere , and at last , tired of roaming through empty rooms and galleries , he stopped in a room smaller than the rest , where a clear fire was burning and a couch was drawn up closely to it .
4 Thinking that this must be prepared for someone who was expected , he sat down to wait till he should come , and very soon fell into a sweet sleep .
5 When his extreme hunger wakened him after several hours , he was still alone ; but a little table , upon which was a good dinner , had been drawn up close to him , and , as he had eaten nothing for twenty-four hours , he lost no time in beginning his meal , hoping that he might soon have an opportunity of thanking his considerate entertainer , whoever it might be .
6 But no one appeared , and even after another long sleep , from which he awoke completely refreshed , there was no sign of anybody , though a fresh meal of dainty cakes and fruit was prepared upon the little table at his elbow .
7 Being naturally timid , the silence began to terrify him , and he resolved to search once more through all the rooms ; but it was of no use .
8 Not even a servant was to be seen ; there was no sign of life in the palace !
9 He began to wonder what he should do , and to amuse himself by pretending that all the treasures he saw were his own , and considering how he would divide them among his children .

1 Now he thought he would saddle it for his homeward journey , and he turned down the path which led to the stable .
2 This path had a hedge of roses on each side of it , and the merchant thought he had never seen or smelt such exquisite flowers .
3 They reminded him of his promise to Beauty , and he stopped and had just gathered one to take to her when he was startled by a strange noise behind him .
4 Turning round , he saw a frightful Beast , which seemed to be very angry and said , in a terrible voice : `` Who told you that you might gather my roses ?
5 Was it not enough that I allowed you to be in my palace and was kind to you ?
6 This is the way you show your gratitude , by stealing my flowers !
7 But your insolence shall not go unpunished . ''
8 The merchant , terrified by these furious words , dropped the fatal rose , and , throwing himself on his knees , cried : `` Pardon me , noble sir .
9 I am truly grateful to you for your hospitality , which was so magnificent that I could not imagine that you would be offended by my taking such a little thing as a rose . ''
10 But the Beast 's anger was not lessened by this speech .
11 `` You are very ready with excuses and flattery , '' he cried ; `` but that will not save you from the death you deserve . ''
12 `` Alas ! ''
13 thought the merchant , `` if my daughter could only know what danger her rose has brought me into ! ''
14 And in despair he began to tell the Beast all his misfortunes , and the reason of his journey , not forgetting to mention Beauty 's request .

2 The Beast considered for a moment , and then he said , in a less furious tone : `` I will forgive you on one condition -- that is , that you will give me one of your daughters . ''
3 `` Ah ! ''
4 cried the merchant , `` if I were cruel enough to buy my own life at the expense of one of my children 's , what excuse could I invent to bring her here ? ''
5 `` No excuse would be necessary , '' answered the Beast .
6 `` If she comes at all she must come willingly .
7 On no other condition will I have her .
8 See if any one of them is courageous enough , and loves you well enough to come and save your life .
9 You seem to be an honest man , so I will trust you to go home .
10 I give you a month to see if either of your daughters will come back with you and stay here , to let you go free .
11 If neither of them is willing , you must come alone , after bidding them good-by for ever , for then you will belong to me .
12 And do not imagine that you can hide from me , for if you fail to keep your word I will come and fetch you ! ''
13 added the Beast grimly .
14 The merchant accepted this proposal , though he did not really think any of his daughters could be persuaded to come .
15 He promised to return at the time appointed , and then , anxious to escape from the presence of the Beast , he asked permission to set off at once .
16 But the Beast answered that he could not go until next day .
17 `` Then you will find a horse ready for you , '' he said .
18 `` Now go and eat your supper , and await my orders . ''
19 The poor merchant , more dead than alive , went back to his room , where the most delicious supper was already served on the little table which was drawn up before a blazing fire .
20 But he was too terrified to eat , and only tasted a few of the dishes , for fear the Beast should be angry if he did not obey his orders .
21 When he had finished he heard a great noise in the next room , which he knew meant that the XXXXX was coming .	Beast		Beast|daughters|dishes|excuse|home|horse|life|man|moment|table

18 The merchant was only too glad when the Beast went away , and though he could not sleep for sadness , he lay down until the sun rose .
19 Then , after a hasty breakfast , he went to gather Beauty 's rose , and mounted his horse , which carried him off so swiftly that in an instant he had lost sight of the palace , and he was still wrapped in gloomy thoughts when it stopped before the door of the cottage .
20 His sons and daughters , who had been very uneasy at his long absence , rushed to meet him , eager to know the result of his journey , which , seeing him mounted upon a splendid horse and wrapped in a rich mantle , they supposed to be favorable .
21 He hid the truth from them at first , only saying sadly to XXXXX as he gave her the rose : `` Here is what you asked me to bring you ; you little know what it has cost . ''	Beauty		Beauty|courtyard|journey|mantle|merchant|noise|permission|proposal|result|sadness

1 The merchant accepted this proposal , though he did not really think any of his daughters could be persuaded to come .
2 He promised to return at the time appointed , and then , anxious to escape from the presence of the Beast , he asked permission to set off at once .
3 But the Beast answered that he could not go until next day .
4 `` Then you will find a horse ready for you , '' he said .
5 `` Now go and eat your supper , and await my orders . ''
6 The poor merchant , more dead than alive , went back to his room , where the most delicious supper was already served on the little table which was drawn up before a blazing fire .
7 But he was too terrified to eat , and only tasted a few of the dishes , for fear the Beast should be angry if he did not obey his orders .
8 When he had finished he heard a great noise in the next room , which he knew meant that the Beast was coming .
9 As he could do nothing to escape his visit , the only thing that remained was to seem as little afraid as possible ; so when the Beast appeared and asked roughly if he had supped well , the merchant answered humbly that he had , thanks to his host 's kindness .
10 Then the Beast warned him to remember their agreement , and to prepare his daughter exactly for what she had to expect .
11 `` Do not get up to-morrow , '' he added , `` until you see the sun and hear a golden bell ring .
12 Then you will find your breakfast waiting for you here , and the horse you are to ride will be ready in the courtyard .
13 He will also bring you back again when you come with your daughter a month hence .
14 Farewell .
15 Take a rose to Beauty , and remember your promise ! ''
16 The merchant was only too glad when the Beast went away , and though he could not sleep for sadness , he lay down until the sun rose .
17 Then , after a hasty breakfast , he went to gather Beauty 's rose , and mounted his horse , which carried him off so swiftly that in an instant he had lost sight of the palace , and he was still wrapped in gloomy thoughts when it stopped before the door of the cottage .
18 His sons and daughters , who had been very uneasy at his long absence , rushed to meet him , eager to know the result of his journey , which , seeing him mounted upon a splendid horse and wrapped in a rich mantle , they supposed to be favorable .
19 He hid the truth from them at first , only saying sadly to Beauty as he gave her the rose : `` Here is what you asked me to bring you ; you little know what it has cost . ''
20 But this excited their curiosity so greatly that presently he told them his adventures from beginning to end , and then they were all very unhappy .
21 The girls lamented loudly over their lost hopes , and the XXXXX declared that their father should not return to this terrible castle , and began to make plans for killing the Beast if it should come to fetch him .	sons		day|journey|merchant|month|presence|result|rose|sons|table|truth

7 Then , after a hasty breakfast , he went to gather Beauty 's rose , and mounted his horse , which carried him off so swiftly that in an instant he had lost sight of the palace , and he was still wrapped in gloomy thoughts when it stopped before the door of the cottage .
8 His sons and daughters , who had been very uneasy at his long absence , rushed to meet him , eager to know the result of his journey , which , seeing him mounted upon a splendid horse and wrapped in a rich mantle , they supposed to be favorable .
9 He hid the truth from them at first , only saying sadly to Beauty as he gave her the rose : `` Here is what you asked me to bring you ; you little know what it has cost . ''
10 But this excited their curiosity so greatly that presently he told them his adventures from beginning to end , and then they were all very unhappy .
11 The girls lamented loudly over their lost hopes , and the sons declared that their father should not return to this terrible castle , and began to make plans for killing the Beast if it should come to fetch him .
12 But he reminded them that he had promised to go back .
13 Then the girls were very angry with Beauty , and said it was all her fault , and that if she had asked for something sensible this would never have happened , and complained bitterly that they should have to suffer for her folly .
14 Poor Beauty , much distressed , said to them : `` I have , indeed , caused this misfortune , but I assure you I did it innocently .
15 Who could have guessed that to ask for a rose in the middle of summer would cause so much misery ?
16 But as I did the mischief it is only just that I should suffer for it .
17 I will therefore go back with my father to keep his promise . ''
18 At first nobody would hear of this arrangement , and her father and brothers , who loved her dearly , declared that nothing should make them let her go ; but Beauty was firm .
19 As the time drew near she divided all her little possessions between her sisters , and said good-by to everything she loved , and when the fatal day came she encouraged and cheered her father as they mounted together the horse which had brought him back .
20 It seemed to fly rather than gallop , but so smoothly that Beauty was not frightened ; indeed , she would have enjoyed the journey if she had not feared what might happen to her at the end of it .
21 Her XXXXX still tried to persuade her to go back , but in vain .	father		Farewell|absence|brothers|father|horse|instant|merchant|plans|possessions|result

5 His sons and daughters , who had been very uneasy at his long absence , rushed to meet him , eager to know the result of his journey , which , seeing him mounted upon a splendid horse and wrapped in a rich mantle , they supposed to be favorable .
6 He hid the truth from them at first , only saying sadly to Beauty as he gave her the rose : `` Here is what you asked me to bring you ; you little know what it has cost . ''
7 But this excited their curiosity so greatly that presently he told them his adventures from beginning to end , and then they were all very unhappy .
8 The girls lamented loudly over their lost hopes , and the sons declared that their father should not return to this terrible castle , and began to make plans for killing the Beast if it should come to fetch him .
9 But he reminded them that he had promised to go back .
10 Then the girls were very angry with Beauty , and said it was all her fault , and that if she had asked for something sensible this would never have happened , and complained bitterly that they should have to suffer for her folly .
11 Poor Beauty , much distressed , said to them : `` I have , indeed , caused this misfortune , but I assure you I did it innocently .
12 Who could have guessed that to ask for a rose in the middle of summer would cause so much misery ?
13 But as I did the mischief it is only just that I should suffer for it .
14 I will therefore go back with my father to keep his promise . ''
15 At first nobody would hear of this arrangement , and her father and brothers , who loved her dearly , declared that nothing should make them let her go ; but Beauty was firm .
16 As the time drew near she divided all her little possessions between her sisters , and said good-by to everything she loved , and when the fatal day came she encouraged and cheered her father as they mounted together the horse which had brought him back .
17 It seemed to fly rather than gallop , but so smoothly that Beauty was not frightened ; indeed , she would have enjoyed the journey if she had not feared what might happen to her at the end of it .
18 Her father still tried to persuade her to go back , but in vain .

20 This lasted until they reached the avenue of orange trees , where were statues holding flaming torches , and when they got nearer to the palace they saw that it was illuminated from the roof to the ground , and music sounded softly from the courtyard .

1 The merchant was only too glad when the Beast went away , and though he could not sleep for sadness , he lay down until the sun rose .
2 Then , after a hasty breakfast , he went to gather Beauty 's rose , and mounted his horse , which carried him off so swiftly that in an instant he had lost sight of the palace , and he was still wrapped in gloomy thoughts when it stopped before the door of the cottage .
3 His sons and daughters , who had been very uneasy at his long absence , rushed to meet him , eager to know the result of his journey , which , seeing him mounted upon a splendid horse and wrapped in a rich mantle , they supposed to be favorable .
4 He hid the truth from them at first , only saying sadly to Beauty as he gave her the rose : `` Here is what you asked me to bring you ; you little know what it has cost . ''
5 But this excited their curiosity so greatly that presently he told them his adventures from beginning to end , and then they were all very unhappy .
6 The girls lamented loudly over their lost hopes , and the sons declared that their father should not return to this terrible castle , and began to make plans for killing the Beast if it should come to fetch him .
7 But he reminded them that he had promised to go back .
8 Then the girls were very angry with Beauty , and said it was all her fault , and that if she had asked for something sensible this would never have happened , and complained bitterly that they should have to suffer for her folly .
9 Poor Beauty , much distressed , said to them : `` I have , indeed , caused this misfortune , but I assure you I did it innocently .
10 Who could have guessed that to ask for a rose in the middle of summer would cause so much misery ?
11 But as I did the mischief it is only just that I should suffer for it .
12 I will therefore go back with my father to keep his promise . ''
13 At first nobody would hear of this arrangement , and her father and brothers , who loved her dearly , declared that nothing should make them let her go ; but Beauty was firm .
14 As the time drew near she divided all her little possessions between her sisters , and said good-by to everything she loved , and when the fatal day came she encouraged and cheered her father as they mounted together the horse which had brought him back .
15 It seemed to fly rather than gallop , but so smoothly that Beauty was not frightened ; indeed , she would have enjoyed the journey if she had not feared what might happen to her at the end of it .
16 Her father still tried to persuade her to go back , but in vain .
17 While they were talking the night fell , and then , to their great surprise , wonderful colored lights began to shine in all directions , and splendid fireworks blazed out before them ; all the forest was illuminated by them , and even felt pleasantly warm , though it had been bitterly cold before .
18 This lasted until they reached the avenue of orange trees , where were statues holding flaming torches , and when they got nearer to the palace they saw that it was illuminated from the roof to the ground , and music sounded softly from the courtyard .
19 `` The Beast must be very hungry , '' said Beauty , trying to laugh , `` if he makes all this rejoicing over the arrival of his prey . ''
20 But , in spite of her anxiety , she could not help admiring all the wonderful things she saw .

1 But this excited their curiosity so greatly that presently he told them his adventures from beginning to end , and then they were all very unhappy .
2 The girls lamented loudly over their lost hopes , and the sons declared that their father should not return to this terrible castle , and began to make plans for killing the Beast if it should come to fetch him .
3 But he reminded them that he had promised to go back .
4 Then the girls were very angry with Beauty , and said it was all her fault , and that if she had asked for something sensible this would never have happened , and complained bitterly that they should have to suffer for her folly .
5 Poor Beauty , much distressed , said to them : `` I have , indeed , caused this misfortune , but I assure you I did it innocently .
6 Who could have guessed that to ask for a rose in the middle of summer would cause so much misery ?
7 But as I did the mischief it is only just that I should suffer for it .
8 I will therefore go back with my father to keep his promise . ''
9 At first nobody would hear of this arrangement , and her father and brothers , who loved her dearly , declared that nothing should make them let her go ; but Beauty was firm .
10 As the time drew near she divided all her little possessions between her sisters , and said good-by to everything she loved , and when the fatal day came she encouraged and cheered her father as they mounted together the horse which had brought him back .
11 It seemed to fly rather than gallop , but so smoothly that Beauty was not frightened ; indeed , she would have enjoyed the journey if she had not feared what might happen to her at the end of it .
12 Her father still tried to persuade her to go back , but in vain .
13 While they were talking the night fell , and then , to their great surprise , wonderful colored lights began to shine in all directions , and splendid fireworks blazed out before them ; all the forest was illuminated by them , and even felt pleasantly warm , though it had been bitterly cold before .
14 This lasted until they reached the avenue of orange trees , where were statues holding flaming torches , and when they got nearer to the palace they saw that it was illuminated from the roof to the ground , and music sounded softly from the courtyard .
15 `` The Beast must be very hungry , '' said Beauty , trying to laugh , `` if he makes all this rejoicing over the arrival of his prey . ''
16 But , in spite of her anxiety , she could not help admiring all the wonderful things she saw .
17 The horse stopped at the foot of the flight of steps leading to the terrace , and when they had dismounted her father led her to the little room he had been in before , where they found a splendid fire burning , and the table daintily spread with a delicious supper .
18 The merchant knew that this was meant for them , and Beauty , who was rather less frightened now that she had passed through so many rooms and seen nothing of the Beast , was quite willing to begin , for her long ride had made her very hungry .
19 But they had hardly finished their meal when the noise of the Beast 's footsteps was heard approaching , and Beauty clung to her father in terror , which became all the greater when she saw how frightened he was .
20 But when the Beast really appeared , though she trembled at the sight of him , she made a great effort to hide her terror , and saluted him respectfully .
21 This evidently pleased the XXXXX .	Beast		Beast|father|firm|folly|journey|merchant|noise|nothing|statues|torches

1 The girls lamented loudly over their lost hopes , and the sons declared that their father should not return to this terrible castle , and began to make plans for killing the Beast if it should come to fetch him .
2 But he reminded them that he had promised to go back .
3 Then the girls were very angry with Beauty , and said it was all her fault , and that if she had asked for something sensible this would never have happened , and complained bitterly that they should have to suffer for her folly .
4 Poor Beauty , much distressed , said to them : `` I have , indeed , caused this misfortune , but I assure you I did it innocently .
5 Who could have guessed that to ask for a rose in the middle of summer would cause so much misery ?
6 But as I did the mischief it is only just that I should suffer for it .
7 I will therefore go back with my father to keep his promise . ''
8 At first nobody would hear of this arrangement , and her father and brothers , who loved her dearly , declared that nothing should make them let her go ; but Beauty was firm .
9 As the time drew near she divided all her little possessions between her sisters , and said good-by to everything she loved , and when the fatal day came she encouraged and cheered her father as they mounted together the horse which had brought him back .
10 It seemed to fly rather than gallop , but so smoothly that Beauty was not frightened ; indeed , she would have enjoyed the journey if she had not feared what might happen to her at the end of it .
11 Her father still tried to persuade her to go back , but in vain .
12 While they were talking the night fell , and then , to their great surprise , wonderful colored lights began to shine in all directions , and splendid fireworks blazed out before them ; all the forest was illuminated by them , and even felt pleasantly warm , though it had been bitterly cold before .
13 This lasted until they reached the avenue of orange trees , where were statues holding flaming torches , and when they got nearer to the palace they saw that it was illuminated from the roof to the ground , and music sounded softly from the courtyard .
14 `` The Beast must be very hungry , '' said Beauty , trying to laugh , `` if he makes all this rejoicing over the arrival of his prey . ''
15 But , in spite of her anxiety , she could not help admiring all the wonderful things she saw .
16 The horse stopped at the foot of the flight of steps leading to the terrace , and when they had dismounted her father led her to the little room he had been in before , where they found a splendid fire burning , and the table daintily spread with a delicious supper .
17 The merchant knew that this was meant for them , and Beauty , who was rather less frightened now that she had passed through so many rooms and seen nothing of the Beast , was quite willing to begin , for her long ride had made her very hungry .
18 But they had hardly finished their meal when the noise of the Beast 's footsteps was heard approaching , and Beauty clung to her father in terror , which became all the greater when she saw how frightened he was .
19 But when the Beast really appeared , though she trembled at the sight of him , she made a great effort to hide her terror , and saluted him respectfully .
20 This evidently pleased the Beast .
21 After looking at her he said , in a tone that might have struck XXXXX into the boldest heart , though he did not seem to be angry : `` Good-evening , old man .	terror		Beauty|anxiety|arrival|courtyard|firm|foot|forest|nobody|plans|terror

1 While they were talking the night fell , and then , to their great surprise , wonderful colored lights began to shine in all directions , and splendid fireworks blazed out before them ; all the forest was illuminated by them , and even felt pleasantly warm , though it had been bitterly cold before .
2 This lasted until they reached the avenue of orange trees , where were statues holding flaming torches , and when they got nearer to the palace they saw that it was illuminated from the roof to the ground , and music sounded softly from the courtyard .
3 `` The Beast must be very hungry , '' said Beauty , trying to laugh , `` if he makes all this rejoicing over the arrival of his prey . ''
4 But , in spite of her anxiety , she could not help admiring all the wonderful things she saw .
5 The horse stopped at the foot of the flight of steps leading to the terrace , and when they had dismounted her father led her to the little room he had been in before , where they found a splendid fire burning , and the table daintily spread with a delicious supper .
6 The merchant knew that this was meant for them , and Beauty , who was rather less frightened now that she had passed through so many rooms and seen nothing of the Beast , was quite willing to begin , for her long ride had made her very hungry .
7 But they had hardly finished their meal when the noise of the Beast 's footsteps was heard approaching , and Beauty clung to her father in terror , which became all the greater when she saw how frightened he was .
8 But when the Beast really appeared , though she trembled at the sight of him , she made a great effort to hide her terror , and saluted him respectfully .
9 This evidently pleased the Beast .
10 After looking at her he said , in a tone that might have struck terror into the boldest heart , though he did not seem to be angry : `` Good-evening , old man .
11 Good-evening , Beauty . ''
12 The merchant was too terrified to reply , but Beauty answered sweetly : `` Good-evening , Beast . ''
13 `` Have you come willingly ? ''
14 asked the Beast .
15 `` Will you be content to stay here when your father goes away ? ''
16 Beauty answered bravely that she was quite prepared to stay .
17 `` I am pleased with you , '' said the Beast .
18 `` As you have come of your own accord , you may stay .
19 As for you , old man , '' he added , turning to the merchant , `` at sunrise to-morrow you will take your departure .
20 When the bell rings get up quickly and eat your breakfast , and you will find the same horse waiting to take you home ; but remember that you must never expect to see my palace again . ''
21 Then turning to XXXXX , he said : `` Take your father into the next room , and help him to choose everything you think your brothers and sisters would like to have .	Beauty		Beauty|effort|laugh|meal|music|prey|rooms|sight|things|trees

17 Then he went away , after saying , `` Good-by , Beauty ; good-by , old man '' ; and though Beauty was beginning to think with great dismay of her father 's departure , she was afraid to disobey the Beast 's orders ; and they went into the next room , which had shelves and cupboards all round it .
18 They were greatly surprised at the riches it contained .

14 `` I think , father , '' she said , `` that , as the gold will be more useful to you , we had better take out the other things again , and fill the trunks with it . ''
15 So they did this ; but the more they put in the more room there seemed to be , and at last they put back all the jewels and dresses they had taken out , and Beauty even added as many more of the jewels as she could carry at once ; and then the trunks were not too full , but they were so heavy that an elephant could not have carried them !
16 `` The Beast was mocking us , '' cried the merchant ; `` he must have pretended to give us all these things , knowing that I could not carry them away . ''
17 `` Let us wait and see , '' answered Beauty .
18 `` I can not believe that he meant to deceive us .
19 All we can do is to fasten them up and leave them ready . ''
20 So they did this and returned to the little room , where , to their astonishment , they found breakfast ready .
21 The XXXXX ate his with a good appetite , as the Beast 's generosity made him believe that he might perhaps venture to come back soon and see Beauty .	merchant		astonishment|dresses|heaps|merchant|orders|ornaments|queen|shelves|sisters|things

1 `` Will you be content to stay here when your father goes away ? ''
2 Beauty answered bravely that she was quite prepared to stay .
3 `` I am pleased with you , '' said the Beast .
4 `` As you have come of your own accord , you may stay .
5 As for you , old man , '' he added , turning to the merchant , `` at sunrise to-morrow you will take your departure .
6 When the bell rings get up quickly and eat your breakfast , and you will find the same horse waiting to take you home ; but remember that you must never expect to see my palace again . ''
7 Then turning to Beauty , he said : `` Take your father into the next room , and help him to choose everything you think your brothers and sisters would like to have .
8 You will find two traveling-trunks there ; fill them as full as you can .
9 It is only just that you should send them something very precious as a remembrance of yourself . ''
10 Then he went away , after saying , `` Good-by , Beauty ; good-by , old man '' ; and though Beauty was beginning to think with great dismay of her father 's departure , she was afraid to disobey the Beast 's orders ; and they went into the next room , which had shelves and cupboards all round it .
11 They were greatly surprised at the riches it contained .
12 There were splendid dresses fit for a queen , with all the ornaments that were to be worn with them ; and when Beauty opened the cupboards she was quite dazzled by the gorgeous jewels that lay in heaps upon every shelf .
13 After choosing a vast quantity , which she divided between her sisters -- for she had made a heap of the wonderful dresses for each of them -- she opened the last chest , which was full of gold .
14 `` I think , father , '' she said , `` that , as the gold will be more useful to you , we had better take out the other things again , and fill the trunks with it . ''

2 So they did this and returned to the little room , where , to their astonishment , they found breakfast ready .
3 The merchant ate his with a good appetite , as the Beast 's generosity made him believe that he might perhaps venture to come back soon and see Beauty .
4 But she felt sure that her father was leaving her for ever , so she was very sad when the bell rang sharply for the second time , and warned them that the time had come for them to part .
5 They went down into the courtyard , where two horses were waiting , one loaded with the two trunks , the other for him to ride .
6 They were pawing the ground in their impatience to start , and the merchant was forced to bid Beauty a hasty farewell ; and as soon as he was mounted he went off at such a pace that she lost sight of him in an instant .
7 Then Beauty began to cry , and wandered sadly back to her own room .
8 But she soon found that she was very sleepy , and as she had nothing better to do she lay down and instantly fell asleep .
9 And then she dreamed that she was walking by a brook bordered with trees , and lamenting her sad fate , when a young prince , handsomer than anyone she had ever seen , and with a voice that went straight to her heart , came and said to her , `` Ah , Beauty !
10 you are not so unfortunate as you suppose .
11 Here you will be rewarded for all you have suffered elsewhere .
12 Your every wish shall be gratified .
13 Only try to find me out , no matter how I may be disguised , as I love you dearly , and in making me happy you will find your own happiness .
14 Be as true-hearted as you are beautiful , and we shall have nothing left to wish for . ''
15 `` What can I do , Prince , to make you happy ? ''
16 said Beauty .
17 `` Only be grateful , '' he answered , `` and do not trust too much to your eyes .
18 And , above all , do not desert me until you have saved me from my cruel misery . ''

20 Only do not let yourself be deceived by appearances . ''

19 With great delight she slipped the bracelet on her arm , and went on into a gallery of pictures , where she soon found a portrait of the same handsome Prince , as large as life , and so well painted that as she studied it he seemed to smile kindly at her .
20 Tearing herself away from the portrait at last , she passed through into a room which contained every musical instrument under the sun , and here she amused herself for a long while in trying some of them , and singing until she was tired .

6 But dinner does not take very long when you are all by yourself , and very soon she sat down cosily in the corner of a sofa , and began to think about the charming Prince she had seen in her dream .
7 `` He said I could make him happy , '' said Beauty to herself .
8 `` It seems , then , that this horrible Beast keeps him a prisoner .
9 How can I set him free ?

11 I do n't understand it .
12 But , after all , it was only a dream , so why should I trouble myself about it ?

13 However , as he did not seem at all ferocious , and only said gruffly : `` Good-evening , Beauty , '' she answered cheerfully and managed to conceal her terror .
14 Then the Beast asked her how she had been amusing herself , and she told him all the rooms she had seen .
15 Then he asked if she thought she could be happy in his palace ; and Beauty answered that everything was so beautiful that she would be very hard to please if she could not be happy .
16 And after about an hour 's talk Beauty began to think that the Beast was not nearly so terrible as she had supposed at first .

4 With great delight she slipped the bracelet on her arm , and went on into a gallery of pictures , where she soon found a portrait of the same handsome Prince , as large as life , and so well painted that as she studied it he seemed to smile kindly at her .
5 Tearing herself away from the portrait at last , she passed through into a room which contained every musical instrument under the sun , and here she amused herself for a long while in trying some of them , and singing until she was tired .
6 The next room was a library , and she saw everything she had ever wanted to read , as well as everything she had read , and it seemed to her that a whole lifetime would not be enough to even read the names of the books , there were so many .
7 By this time it was growing dusk , and wax candles in diamond and ruby candlesticks were beginning to light themselves in every room .
8 Beauty found her supper served just at the time she preferred to have it , but she did not see anyone or hear a sound , and , though her father had warned her that she would be alone , she began to find it rather dull .
9 But presently she heard the Beast coming , and wondered tremblingly if he meant to eat her up now .
10 However , as he did not seem at all ferocious , and only said gruffly : `` Good-evening , Beauty , '' she answered cheerfully and managed to conceal her terror .
11 Then the Beast asked her how she had been amusing herself , and she told him all the rooms she had seen .
12 Then he asked if she thought she could be happy in his palace ; and Beauty answered that everything was so beautiful that she would be very hard to please if she could not be happy .
13 And after about an hour 's talk Beauty began to think that the Beast was not nearly so terrible as she had supposed at first .
14 Then he got up to leave her , and said in his gruff voice : `` Do you love me , Beauty ?
15 Will you marry me ? ''
16 `` Oh !
17 what shall I say ? ''
18 cried Beauty , for she was afraid to make the Beast angry by refusing .
19 `` Say ` yes ' or ` no ' without fear , '' he replied .
20 `` Oh !
21 no , Beast , '' said XXXXX hastily .	Beauty		Beauty|anyone|dusk|fear|lifetime|rooms|singing|sun|voice|while

1 what shall I say ? ''
2 cried Beauty , for she was afraid to make the Beast angry by refusing .
3 `` Say ` yes ' or ` no ' without fear , '' he replied .
4 `` Oh !
5 no , Beast , '' said Beauty hastily .
6 `` Since you will not , good-night , Beauty , '' he said .
7 And she answered , `` Good-night , Beast , '' very glad to find that her refusal had not provoked him .
8 And after he was gone she was very soon in bed and asleep , and dreaming of her unknown Prince .
9 She thought he came and said to her : `` Ah , Beauty !
10 why are you so unkind to me ?
11 I fear I am fated to be unhappy for many a long day still . ''
12 And then her dreams changed , but the charming Prince figured in them all ; and when morning came her first thought was to look at the portrait , and see if it was really like him , and she found that it certainly was .
13 This morning she decided to amuse herself in the garden , for the sun shone , and all the fountains were playing ; but she was astonished to find that every place was familiar to her , and presently she came to the brook where the myrtle trees were growing where she had first met the Prince in her dream , and that made her think more than ever that he must be kept a prisoner by the Beast .
14 When she was tired she went back to the palace , and found a new room full of materials for every kind of work -- ribbons to make into bows , and silks to work into flowers .
15 Then there was an aviary full of rare birds , which were so tame that they flew to Beauty as soon as they saw her , and perched upon her shoulders and her head .
16 `` Pretty little creatures , '' she said , `` how I wish that your cage was nearer to my room , that I might often hear you sing ! ''
17 So saying she opened a door , and found , to her delight , that it led into her own room , though she had thought it was quite the other side of the palace .
18 There were more birds in a room farther on , parrots and cockatoos that could talk , and they greeted Beauty by name ; indeed , she found them so entertaining that she took one or two back to her room , and they talked to her while she was at supper ; after which the Beast paid her his usual visit , and asked her the same questions as before , and then with a gruff `` good-night '' he took his departure , and Beauty went to bed to dream of her mysterious Prince .
19 The days passed swiftly in different amusements , and after a while Beauty found out another strange thing in the palace , which often pleased her when she was tired of being alone .
20 There was one room which she had not noticed particularly ; it was empty , except that under each of the windows stood a very comfortable chair ; and the first time she had looked out of the window it had seemed to her that a black curtain prevented her from seeing anything outside .
21 But the second time she went into the XXXXX , happening to be tired , she sat down in one of the chairs , when instantly the curtain was rolled aside , and a most amusing pantomime was acted before her ; there were dances , and colored lights , and music , and pretty dresses , and it was all so gay that Beauty was in ecstacies .	room		bed|creatures|curtain|garden|head|refusal|room|time|window|windows

13 This morning she decided to amuse herself in the garden , for the sun shone , and all the fountains were playing ; but she was astonished to find that every place was familiar to her , and presently she came to the brook where the myrtle trees were growing where she had first met the Prince in her dream , and that made her think more than ever that he must be kept a prisoner by the Beast .
14 When she was tired she went back to the palace , and found a new room full of materials for every kind of work -- ribbons to make into bows , and silks to work into flowers .

16 `` Pretty little creatures , '' she said , `` how I wish that your cage was nearer to my room , that I might often hear you sing ! ''
17 So saying she opened a door , and found , to her delight , that it led into her own room , though she had thought it was quite the other side of the palace .
18 There were more birds in a room farther on , parrots and cockatoos that could talk , and they greeted Beauty by name ; indeed , she found them so entertaining that she took one or two back to her room , and they talked to her while she was at supper ; after which the Beast paid her his usual visit , and asked her the same questions as before , and then with a gruff `` good-night '' he took his departure , and Beauty went to bed to dream of her mysterious Prince .

1 `` Say ` yes ' or ` no ' without fear , '' he replied .
2 `` Oh !
3 no , Beast , '' said Beauty hastily .
4 `` Since you will not , good-night , Beauty , '' he said .
5 And she answered , `` Good-night , Beast , '' very glad to find that her refusal had not provoked him .
6 And after he was gone she was very soon in bed and asleep , and dreaming of her unknown Prince .
7 She thought he came and said to her : `` Ah , Beauty !
8 why are you so unkind to me ?
9 I fear I am fated to be unhappy for many a long day still . ''
10 And then her dreams changed , but the charming Prince figured in them all ; and when morning came her first thought was to look at the portrait , and see if it was really like him , and she found that it certainly was .
11 This morning she decided to amuse herself in the garden , for the sun shone , and all the fountains were playing ; but she was astonished to find that every place was familiar to her , and presently she came to the brook where the myrtle trees were growing where she had first met the Prince in her dream , and that made her think more than ever that he must be kept a prisoner by the Beast .
12 When she was tired she went back to the palace , and found a new room full of materials for every kind of work -- ribbons to make into bows , and silks to work into flowers .
13 Then there was an aviary full of rare birds , which were so tame that they flew to Beauty as soon as they saw her , and perched upon her shoulders and her head .
14 `` Pretty little creatures , '' she said , `` how I wish that your cage was nearer to my room , that I might often hear you sing ! ''
15 So saying she opened a door , and found , to her delight , that it led into her own room , though she had thought it was quite the other side of the palace .
16 There were more birds in a room farther on , parrots and cockatoos that could talk , and they greeted Beauty by name ; indeed , she found them so entertaining that she took one or two back to her room , and they talked to her while she was at supper ; after which the Beast paid her his usual visit , and asked her the same questions as before , and then with a gruff `` good-night '' he took his departure , and Beauty went to bed to dream of her mysterious Prince .
17 The days passed swiftly in different amusements , and after a while Beauty found out another strange thing in the palace , which often pleased her when she was tired of being alone .
18 There was one room which she had not noticed particularly ; it was empty , except that under each of the windows stood a very comfortable chair ; and the first time she had looked out of the window it had seemed to her that a black curtain prevented her from seeing anything outside .
19 But the second time she went into the room , happening to be tired , she sat down in one of the chairs , when instantly the curtain was rolled aside , and a most amusing pantomime was acted before her ; there were dances , and colored lights , and music , and pretty dresses , and it was all so gay that Beauty was in ecstacies .
20 After that she tried the other seven windows in turn , and there was some new and surprising entertainment to be seen from each of them , so that Beauty never could feel lonely any more .
21 Every evening after supper the XXXXX came to see her , and always before saying good-night asked her in his terrible voice : `` Beauty , will you marry me ? ''	Beast		Beast|Beauty|amusements|anything|cage|dresses|fear|good-night|room|side
